    "by definition cross product bialgebras are isomorphic to factorizations @xmath0 , in a braided category say , such that the given isomorphisms can be characterized universally in terms of certain projections and injections from the bialgebra into the particular tensor factors . in this context tensor",
    "product bialgebras , bi- or bismash product bialgebras @xcite , doublecross product bialgebras , bicross product bialgebras and double biproduct bialgebras @xcite are cross product bialgebras . but also the bicrossed or cocycle bicross product bialgebras @xcite are cross product bialgebras in our terminology ; their universal characterization is given in terms of cleft extensions and coextensions ( see @xcite for a comprehensive study of cleft or normal basis hopf - galois extensions on the algebra level ) .",
    "the notion of cross product bialgebras therefore as well includes constructions involving cocycles and dual cocycles ( or simply `` cycles '' ) .",
    "well known examples of cross product bialgebras are drinfeld s quantum double , the quantum poincar group , radford s 4-parameter hopf algebra , lusztig s construction of the quantum enveloping algebra , the quantum weyl group , the affine quantum groups @xmath1 , the connes - moscovici hopf algebra in transverse differential geometry @xcite , etc .",
    "the universal constructions of cross product bialgebras in @xcite additionally admit an equivalent characterization in terms of mutual weak ( co-)modular , co - cyclic relations of the tensor factors @xmath2 and @xmath3 .",
    "this means that there exist certain weak ( co-)multiplications , ( co-)cycles and ( co-)actions which are morphisms with tensor rank @xmath4 or @xmath5 defined on @xmath2 and @xmath3 and their two - fold tensor products , such that the multiplication @xmath6 and the comultiplication @xmath7 of the bialgebra @xmath8 can be composed monoidally by these structure morphisms .",
    "for example we encounter a weak left coaction @xmath9 which has tensor rank @xmath5 , a weak cocycle @xmath10 with rank @xmath4 , etc .",
    "all these structure morphisms are subject to certain relations with rank @xmath11 , @xmath12 and @xmath13 which on the one hand follow from the bialgebra structure of @xmath0 and on the other hand determine the bialgebra structure of @xmath14 uniquely .    despite those common properties of the cross product bialgebra constructions in @xcite no theory exists which characterizes all of them as special versions of a single universal construction which in turn is uniquely determined by its ( co-)modular co - cyclic structure .",
    "a first step towards this objective has been achieved in @xcite where we discovered a method to describe cross product bialgebras without co - cycles , generalizing and uniting @xcite .",
    "the present article considerably extends the results of @xcite .",
    "the main outcome is a universal and ( co-)modular , co - cyclic theory of cross product bialgebras with cocycles and cycles which unites all known constructions within a single setting and provides several new families of cross product bialgebras .",
    "this is the most comprising framework for cross product bialgebras so far , which equivalently takes into account both universal and ( co-)modular co - cyclic aspects .",
    "furthermore our construction is designed to work in arbitrary braided categories .    to derive these results",
    "we will proceed in two steps .",
    "we begin with the general definition of cross product bialgebras and find a universal characterization for them .",
    "we show that so - called cocycle cross product bialgebras possess a certain ( co-)modular co - cyclic structure .",
    "then we restrict our consideration to strong cross product bialgebras .",
    "they also admit a universal characterization and will turn out to be the central objects in our theory of cross product bialgebras .    in a second step",
    "we present a ( co-)modular co - cyclic construction method by so - called hopf data .",
    "a hopf datum consists of a pair of objects @xmath15 and weak ( co-)actions , ( co-)multiplications and co - cycles defined on @xmath2 and @xmath3 which obey certain interrelated identities with rank @xmath11 , @xmath12 and @xmath13 .",
    "then we introduce strong hopf data for which additional `` strong '' relations hold .",
    "we show that strong hopf data induce the structure of a strong cross product bialgebra on the tensor product @xmath14 .",
    "strong hopf data and strong cross product bialgebras are different depictions of the same object .    then we combine the universal characterization and the ( co-)modular co - cyclic description in terms of strong hopf data to obtain the theory of strong cross product bialgebras .",
    "this is the central result of the article .",
    "eventually we apply our construction and investigate strong cross product bialgebras according to their ( co-)modular co - cyclic structure .",
    "in particular we recover all known constructions @xcite and find various new types of cross product bialgebras .",
    "all of them are special versions of the most general strong cross product bialgebra construction .",
    "0.3 cm    after introducing preliminary notations and definitions we study cross product algebras and cross product coalgebras from a universal point of view in section [ sec - ccpa ] .",
    "these results will be used in section [ sec - ccpb ] to define cross product bialgebras . from this general definition",
    "we extract cocycle cross product bialgebras and strong cross product bialgebras .",
    "the structure of cocycle cross product bialgebras gives useful hints for the design of hopf data .",
    "this will be done in section [ hopf - data ] where we investigate the connection of hopf data and cocycle cross product bialgebras .",
    "a hopf datum is canonically assigned to every cocycle cross product bialgebra .",
    "the converse is not true in general . but",
    "theorem [ hp - cp ] states that strong hopf data yield strong cross product bialgebras .",
    "more precisely strong hopf data and strong cross product bialgebras are equivalent constructions which are in one - to - one correspondence",
    ". the universal ( co-)modular co - cyclic theory of strong cross product bialgebras culminates in the central theorems [ hp - cp ] and [ central - theory ] .",
    "finally we present a table of special strong cross product bialgebras which contains all known and several new types of cross product bialgebras embedded in our most general framework .",
    "the rather intricate proof of theorem [ hp - cp ] has been postponed to section [ proof - hp - cp ] .",
    "0.3 cm    in the recent articles @xcite cross product bialgebras have been studied as well . in @xcite the universal properties of co - cycle free cross product bialgebras have been considered .",
    "the article @xcite investigates certain cross product bialgebras without co - cycles in universal and ( co-)modular co - cyclic terms .",
    "in @xcite a special type of our cocycle cross product bialgebras with one cocycle has been studied in the special case where all objects are vector spaces over a field .",
    "we are working throughout in ( strict ) braided monoidal categories @xcite . in our article",
    "we denote categories by calligraphic letters @xmath16 , @xmath17 , etc . for a braided monoidal category @xmath16 the tensor product",
    "is denoted by @xmath18 , the unit object by @xmath19 , and the braiding by @xmath20 . if it is clear from the context we omit the index ` @xmath16 ' at the various symbols .",
    "we confine ourselves to braided categories which admit split idempotents @xcite ; for each idempotent @xmath21 of any object @xmath22 in @xmath16 there exists an object @xmath23 and a pair of morphisms @xmath24 such that @xmath25 and @xmath26 .",
    "this is not a severe restriction of the categories since every braided category can be canonically embedded into a braided category which admits split idempotents @xcite .",
    "we use generalized algebraic structures like algebra , bialgebra , module , comodule , etc .",
    "in such categories . we assume the reader is familiar with these generalizations .",
    "a thorough introduction to braided algebraic structures and the graphical calculus coming along with it can be found in @xcite .",
    "we denote by @xmath27 the multiplication and by @xmath28 the unit of an algebra @xmath29 in @xmath16 .",
    "@xmath30 is meant for the comultiplication and @xmath31 for the counit of a coalgebra @xmath32 in @xmath16 , @xmath33 is the left action of an algebra @xmath29 on a module @xmath22 , and @xmath34 denotes the left coaction of a coalgebra @xmath32 on a comodule @xmath35 .",
    "right actions are denoted by @xmath36 and right coactions by @xmath37 .",
    "in the course of our work we often encounter weak versions of ( co-)multiplication and ( co-)action which do not necessarily obey the relations of ` true ' ( co-)algebras and ( co-)modules .",
    "we will nevertheless use the same symbols as for proper ( co-)multiplications and ( co-)actions  it should become clear from the context whether these structure morphisms are weak or not .    in our article we make use of graphical calculus for ( strict ) braided monoidal categories which simplifies intricate categorical equations of morphisms and helps to uncover their intrinsic structure .",
    "morphisms will be composed from up to down , i.  e.  the domains of the morphisms are at the top and the codomaines are at the bottom of the graphics .",
    "tensor products are represented by horizontal concatenation in the corresponding order .",
    "we present our own conventions @xcite in figure [ fig - conv ] .",
    "if there is no fear of confusion we omit the assignment of a specific object to the ends of the particular strings in the graphics .",

    "@xmath171 is a co - smash product coalgebra.to 1em@xmath145    0.3 cm    pi - symwe would like to point out the following important observation to the reader",
    ". definition [ caat ] is not dual to definition [ ccat ] .",
    "rather , both definitions can be obtained from each other by a combination of duality ( followed by the usual exchanges of multiplication and comultiplication , unit and counit , cocycle and cycle , etc . ) and use of the opposite tensor product ( followed by exchange of indices `` 1 @xmath172 2 '' , and later also by exchange of `` left / right ( coaction ) @xmath172 right / left ( action ) '' ) . this is not an accidential fact but has to do with the subsequent definition of cross product bialgebras where we use precisely these algebra and coalgebra structures .",
    "only then are we able to get all the known cross product bialgebras @xcite .",
    "this kind of symmetry between cross product algebra and cross product coalgebra will be called * @xmath173-symmetry * henceforth . in terms of graphical calculus @xmath174-symmetry",
    "can be interpreted easily as rotation of the graphic by the angle @xmath174 along an axis normal to the planar graphic followed by the above mentioned exchanges of indices and morphism types .",
    "we will often apply this principle to obtain @xmath174-symmetric results simply by @xmath174-rotation . hence cross product bialgebras - as defined below - are therefore @xmath174-symmetric invariant rather than dual symmetric invariant .",
    "dualization of our definition would lead to another kind of cross product bialgebras .",
    "the corresponding results for these dual versions follow from our results straightforwardly by dualization .",
    "sec - ccpb    in section [ sec - ccpb ] we investigate cross product bialgebras from a universal point of view .",
    "they are simultaneously cross product algebras and cross product coalgebras with compatible bialgebra structure .",
    "we find a universal description for the isomorphism classes of cross product bialgebras",
    ". then we will consider special cases called cocycle and strong cross product bialgebras which are universal constructions as well .",
    "but in addition the given isomorphism class of a cocycle / strong cross product bialgebra can be characterized by certain interrelated ( co-)modular co - cyclic structures on the tensor factors .",
    "strong cross product bialgebras are the pivotal objects for the studies in section [ hopf - data ] .",

    "0.3 cm    0.3 cm    in the sequel we will consider special versions of strong cross product bialgebras .",
    "they admit equivalent universal and ( co-)modular co - cyclic descriptions and can be derived from the most general construction given in theorem [ hp - cp ] . in particular",
    "all known constructions of cocycle cross product bialgebras will be recovered , and additionally we find several new types of cocycle cross product bialgebras . in proposition [ bialg - cocycle6 ]",

    "the dual strong cross product bialgebras will be denoted by a classification box @xmath441 with entries @xmath443 for the ( co)actions , @xmath445 for the cocycle @xmath286 , and @xmath444 for the cycle @xmath287 .",
    "then analogously @xmath450 special types of dual strong cross product bialgebras can be obtained from which @xmath449 ( co - cycle free ) types coincide with the corresponding 16 types of strong cross product bialgebras .",
    "therefore the total number of different types of strong and dual strong cross product bialgebras which is classified by our scheme is @xmath451 .",
    "however , henceforth we do not tell between a certain type and its dual or @xmath174-symmetric counterparts - it is an easy exercise to obtain one from the other - rotation of the classification box in the plane of the graphic yields the corresponding @xmath174-symmetric counterpart of a certain type of cross product bialgebra .",
    "and analogously a reflection of the classification box along a horizontal line yields the dual counterpart . ] . up to this @xmath452-symmetry",
    "we obtain @xmath453 different classification boxes . in figure [ fig - class ]",

    "we found a universal theory of strong cross product bialgebras with an equivalent ( co-)modular co - cyclic characterization in terms of strong hopf data .",
    "the theory unites all known cross product bialgebras @xcite in a single construction .",
    "furthermore various new types of cross product bialgebras arise out of the most general construction .",
    "the ( co-)modular co - cyclic structure of strong cross product bialgebras corresponds canonically to a strong hopf datum which in turn completely determines the bialgebra structure .",
    "thus hopf data basically provide a pattern for the realization of cross product bialgebras in terms of explicit examples - a task to be done in future investigations .",
    "there is no conceptual explanation yet for the understanding of the strong conditions in definition [ strong - hp ] .",
    "a canonical origin of these conditions may be found in higher dimensional categorical constructions of cross product bialgebras where the two tensor factors of the strong cross product bialgebras will be considered as object of two different monoidal categories .",
    "since we are working throughout in braided categories , the results of the article may now be used to investigate cross product bialgebras in various types of braided categories ( see @xcite for applications in hopf bimodule categories ) .",
    "our directions of study of cross product bialgebras are particularly concerned with these questions as well as with extension theory and cohomological considerations ( see @xcite ) .",

  "abstract_text": [
    "<S> this is the central article of a series of three papers on cross product bialgebras . </S>",
    "<S> we present a universal theory of bialgebra factorizations ( or cross product bialgebras ) with cocycles and dual cocycles . </S>",
    "<S> we also provide an equivalent ( co-)modular co - cyclic formulation . </S>",
    "<S> all known examples as for instance bi- or smash , doublecross and bicross product bialgebras as well as double biproduct bialgebras and bicrossed or cocycle bicross product bialgebras are now united within a single theory . furthermore our construction yields various novel types of cross product bialgebras .     </S>",
    "<S> + _ 1991 mathematics subject classification :  _ 16w30 , 16s40 , 18d10 , 16b50 , 81r50 </S>"
  ]
